  <td width="49%" colspan="2" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:49.76%;">
  <p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>
  </td>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<h1 align="center" style="font-weight:normal;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-decoration:underline;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Kraft Foods Inc. Reports First Quarter 2004 Results</font></u></b></h1>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">&#149;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i><font style="font-style:italic;">First Quarter 2004 Diluted E.P.S. Of $0.33 Down 32.7%
Versus 2003 Including $0.12 In Exit Costs For Restructuring Program And An
Intangible Asset Impairment Charge</font></i></p>

<p style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">&#149;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i><font style="font-style:italic;">Net Revenues Up 4.5% On Volume Growth Of 0.5%</font></i></p>

<p align="left" style="font-family:'Times New Roman';margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">&#149;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Sustainable
Growth Plan On Track</font></i></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">NORTHFIELD, IL
&#150; April 19, 2004 &#150; Kraft Foods Inc. (NYSE: KFT) today reported first quarter
2004 results.&#160; Diluted earnings per
share of $0.33 were in line with expectations and down 32.7% versus 2003 due
largely to $0.12 per share in exit costs for the restructuring program
announced in January and an intangible asset impairment charge.&#160; The company indicated that it expects
full-year earnings per share to be in line with current Street estimates and at
the lower end of its EPS guidance range of $1.63-$1.70 (which includes an
estimated $0.30 per share in asset impairment charges and exit costs for the
restructuring program), due primarily to higher than originally anticipated
commodity costs.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#147;As expected, the company&#146;s first quarter earnings were down versus
prior year due to restructuring charges, increased marketing investment and
higher benefit costs,&#148; said Jim Dollive, Chief Financial Officer of Kraft
Foods. &#147;During the quarter, we made good progress on our Sustainable Growth
Plan.&#160; Our increased marketing
investment drove improved results in key businesses, and our cost restructuring
program is on track.&#160; While reported
volume growth was just 0.5%, declines and difficult comparisons in select
categories and countries masked solid growth across much of the portfolio.&#160; Given the early success of these
initiatives, we remain committed to increasing our 2004 marketing investment by
$500-$600 million as a key element of the Sustainable Growth Plan.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Dollive added, &#147;Costs of many commodities surged during the quarter,
most notably U.S. cheese costs, which reached historical highs.&#160; These higher costs are expected to be a key
challenge for both Kraft and the food industry.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<h6 align="center" style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;text-decoration:underline;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">First Quarter Results</font></u></b></h6>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Diluted earnings per share were in line with the company&#146;s previous
guidance and were down 32.7% versus the prior year, as a decline in operating
income of 33.5% was partly offset by reduced interest expense and a lower
effective tax rate.&#160; Earnings per share
were impacted by exit costs for the restructuring</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">1</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='1',FILE='C:\jms\eudelhofen\04-4571-1\task110594\4571-1-mm.htm',USER='eudelho',CD='Apr 19 11:31 2004' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">program ($0.11
per share), higher commodity costs ($0.05 per share), increased marketing
investment ($0.03 per share), increased benefit costs and restricted stock
expense ($0.02 per share), and an intangible asset impairment charge ($0.01 per
share), partially offset by a lower tax rate ($0.02 per share), favorable
currency ($0.01 per share) and growth from the remainder of operations ($0.03
per share), including top-line growth. </font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net revenues in the first quarter increased $334 million, or 4.5%, due
to favorable currency of $306 million and volume growth.&#160; Total reported volume was up 0.5% due to
ongoing volume growth of 0.8%, partially offset by the impact of
divestitures.&#160; Volume strength across
many businesses was partially offset by continued challenges in cookies and
cereals, including the low carbohydrate diet phenomenon; by trade inventory
reductions in certain categories and countries; and by tough comparisons with last
year, when new product activity was skewed to the first quarter.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kraft North America Commercial (KNAC) volume growth of 1.0% was
broad-based, with strength in foodservice, cheese, snack nuts, meats, desserts,
and enhancers, partially offset by weakness in cookies and cereal as well as
new product timing and trade inventory reductions on ready-to-drink
beverages.&#160; Volume in non-measured
channels was up double digits across most businesses.&#160; Volume at Kraft International Commercial (KIC) decreased 0.9%, as
the impact of divested businesses more than offset on-going volume growth of
0.4%.&#160; Ongoing volume growth was driven
by tack-on acquisitions and growth in the UK and Germany, partially offset by
declines in France and Puerto Rico, due to aggressive price competition, and in
Russia due to trade inventory reductions.&#160;
Other key developing markets, such as China, Venezuela, Argentina and
Brazil, all recorded solid volume increases in the quarter.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The company&#146;s Sustainable
Growth Plan progressed on track during the quarter.&#160; Marketing investment increased by approximately $75 million
versus the prior year.&#160; The marketing
increase in the first quarter was focused in three U.S. categories: cheese,
cold cuts and snack nuts.&#160; In cheese and
cold cuts, consumption and share trends remained strong.&#160; Snack nuts consumption and volume were both
up double digits, benefiting from consumer health and wellness trends.&#160; Consistent with the Sustainable Growth Plan,
increased spending during the remainder of 2004 will be leveraged to manage
price gaps, to increase media spending, to drive growth in developing markets
and non-measured channels, to enhance brand equity and to support new
products.&#160; Recent and upcoming new
product launches include <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">CarbWell </font></b>cereals,
bars and cookies; <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Post Honey Bunches of Oats</font></b>
varieties with Peach and Banana; <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Nabisco</font></b>
100-Calorie Packs; <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Back to Nature</font></b>
expansions into new categories; <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">DiGiorno</font></b>
Thin Crispy Crust Pizza; <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Kool Aid</font></b>
Jammers 10; <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Capri Sun Fruit Waves;</font></b>
new <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Philadelphia</font></b> Cream Cheese
varieties in Germany, Austria and the UK; and <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Milka
</font></b>M-joy in Germany and Austria.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The restructuring program announced in January is on track.&#160; During the first quarter, the company
announced the exit of five plants and the elimination of approximately 2,000
positions worldwide.&#160; Pre-tax</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='2',FILE='C:\jms\eudelhofen\04-4571-1\task110594\4571-1-mm.htm',USER='eudelho',CD='Apr 19 11:31 2004' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">charges from
these actions were $279 million.&#160;
Pre-tax savings from the restructuring program were approximately $10
million for the quarter.&#160; For the full
year, the company projects pre-tax exit costs and all intangible asset charges
of $750-$800 million (after-tax equivalent of approximately $0.30 per share)
and pre-tax savings of $120-$140 million for the restructuring program.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The company completed its annual review of goodwill and intangible
assets during the first quarter.&#160; This
review resulted in a pre-tax $29 million non-cash charge related to an
intangible asset impairment for a small confectionery business in the U.S. and
certain brands in Mexico.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During the quarter, the company declared a regular quarterly dividend
of $0.18 per common share and repurchased 4.9 million shares of Class A common
stock for $162 million.&#160; </font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In March, the company announced the acquisition of Veryfine Products
Inc., the privately held manufacturer of <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Fruit<sub>2</sub>O</font></b>
flavored water and <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Veryfine</font></b> juices
and juice drinks, with 2003 net sales of approximately $140 million.&#160; In early April, the company announced a
licensing agreement with Tazo Tea Company, a wholly owned subsidiary of
Starbucks Corporation, under which Kraft will market, sell and distribute <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Tazo</font></b> products across the entire U.S.
grocery channel.&#160; </font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<h4 align="center" style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;text-decoration:underline;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Outlook</font></u></b></h4>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Diluted earnings per share in 2004 are projected to be in line with
current Street estimates and at the lower end of the company&#146;s previously issued
guidance of $1.63-$1.70, which includes an estimated $0.30 per share impact
from asset impairment charges and exit costs for the restructuring
program.&#160; Key items expected to
adversely impact earnings growth in 2004 include higher commodity costs, increased
marketing and price gap management spending of $500-$600 million ($0.19-$0.23
per share), higher pension and post-employment costs and restricted stock
expense (combined $0.07 per share), and gains on sales of businesses recorded
in 2003 ($0.01 per share).</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Prices for many of the company&#146;s major commodities increased
substantially during the first quarter, most notably dairy, soybean oil, grains
and coffee.&#160; Dairy costs in particular
are expected to remain significantly higher than last year because of lower
U.S. milk supplies.&#160; In response to
higher costs, the company announced increased prices in several of its U.S.
cheese businesses at the end of the first quarter.&#160; Higher commodity costs, particularly dairy, are expected to be a
key challenge in the remainder of the year.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The company projects full-year growth in constant currency revenues of
around 3% (including tack-on acquisitions and excluding the impact of
divestitures).&#160; Top-line growth is
projected to improve during the latter part of the year due to tack-on
acquisitions, the timing of new product launches, substantial increases in
marketing investments and developing market growth.&#160; Beyond top-line growth, other earnings drivers are expected to
include restructuring program savings ($0.05 per share) and a lower effective
tax rate.&#160; The first quarter tax rate of
31.9% was down more than three points versus prior year, reflecting the</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">3</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">favorable
resolution of tax items.&#160; For the full
year, the effective tax rate is expected to average approximately 33.5%.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 3.0pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In the second quarter, three items in particular are expected to
adversely impact earnings.&#160; First, the
quarter contains the highest projected marketing investment of all the
quarters.&#160; Second, short-term margin
compression is anticipated as the benefit of pricing lags commodity cost
increases, particularly in cheese.&#160;
Third, the company expects an effective tax rate of approximately 36.0%
in the quarter.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 2.9pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">As a result of the organization changes
announced on January 8, 2004, the company&#146;s first quarter results are presented
in a new segment structure.&#160; Restated
historical results are available in the financial tables contained in this
release.&#160; The company reports six
segments:&#160; U.S. Beverages &amp; Grocery;
U.S. Snacks; U.S. Cheese, Canada &amp; North America Foodservice; U.S.
Convenient Meals; Europe, Middle East &amp; Africa; and Latin America &amp;
Asia Pacific.&#160; The new segment structure
in North America reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between
segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors.&#160; Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico
businesses, which were previously reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers
segment, are now reported in the Latin America &amp; Asia Pacific segment.</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">As described in &#147;Note 13, Segment Reporting&#148;
of Kraft Foods Inc.&#146;s 2003 Annual Report, management reviews operating
companies income (OCI), which is defined as operating income before corporate
expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and
allocate resources.&#160; Management believes
it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze business
performance and trends.&#160; (For a reconciliation
of OCI to operating income, see the Condensed Statements of Earnings contained
in this release.)</font></i></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">4</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:ideograph-numeric ideograph-other;text-decoration:underline;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kraft
North America Commercial</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Operating companies income declined 33.5% to
$846 million due to exit costs for the restructuring program of $245 million,
higher commodity and benefit costs, increased marketing investment and an
intangible asset impairment charge of $17 million, partially offset by the
contribution from volume growth and favorable currency of $11 million.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net revenues increased 2.5% to $5,399 million
as higher volume, favorable currency of $72 million, and commodity-driven
pricing in foodservice were partially offset by increased promotional
spending.&#160; Volume was up 1.0% behind
solid growth in many businesses, particularly those with higher marketing
spending as part of the Sustainable Growth Plan, offset by declines in biscuits
and cereal and an overall shift in the timing of new products.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Following are first quarter results by
segment for KNAC:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">U.S. Beverages &amp; Grocery</font></u></i>
net revenues decreased 0.7% due primarily to a volume decline of 0.3%.&#160; Volume decreases in Cereal and Beverages
were partially offset by mid-single digit growth in Desserts, Enhancers and
Coffee.&#160; A double digit decline in
Cereal was driven by category softness reflecting consumers&#146; focus on lower
carbohydrate products, the timing of new product launches and aggressive
competition.&#160; Beverages were down due to
the timing of new product launches, related trade inventory reductions and, to
a lesser extent, aggressive price competition.&#160;
Desserts grew behind sugar-free, ready-to-eat desserts and <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Cool Whip</font></b> frozen toppings.&#160; Enhancers growth reflected strong gains in
non-measured channels for <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Kraft</font></b>
salad dressings and mayonnaise.&#160; Despite
a difficult competitive environment, Coffee volume increased behind growth in
non-measured channels.&#160; Segment OCI
decreased 11.9% to $457 million due to exit costs for the restructuring program
of $15 million, increased commodity and benefit costs, and lower volume,
partially offset by a decrease in marketing spending.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="font-family:'Times New Roman';margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">U.S.
Snacks</font></u></i><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;"> net revenues decreased 1.8% due to adverse mix and
flat overall volume, with higher Snack Nuts volume offset by lower Biscuits
volume.&#160; Double digit volume gains in <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Planter&#146;s</font></b> Snack Nuts reflect the growing
consumer awareness of the nutritional benefits of nuts, improved marketing
programs, and higher marketing spending as part of the Sustainable Growth
Plan.&#160; In Biscuits, consumers&#146; focus on
low carbohydrate diets continued to affect consumption in the first
quarter.&#160; Cookie share was down just
slightly, while cracker share was up one point.&#160; Within crackers, <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Ritz </font></b>Chips
continued to perform well.&#160; Segment OCI
declined to a $15 million loss due to exit costs for the restructuring program
of $159 million, increased commodity and benefit costs, an intangible asset
impairment charge of $17 million (for a small confectionery business), and
adverse product mix, partially offset by reduced product returns.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">U.S. Cheese, Canada &amp; North America
Foodservice</font></u></i> net revenues increased 10.1% driven by
volume growth, favorable currency of $72 million and Foodservice pricing,
partially offset by higher</p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">5</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;">&nbsp;</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">promotional reinvestment spending in Cheese.&#160; Volume was up 3.9% driven by growth in Foodservice due to strong
national account results and by mid-single digit growth in Cheese, as
Sustainable Growth Plan reinvestment spending is having its intended
effect.&#160; Shares improved in all key
cheese segments, including Naturals (+1.0 points), Cream Cheese (+3.8 points)
and Process Slices (+2.5 points).&#160;
Segment OCI declined 34.1% to $207 million as exit costs for the
restructuring program of $62 million, increased commodity and benefit costs,
and higher marketing spending were partially offset by volume growth and favorable
currency of $11 million.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">U.S. Convenient Meals</font></u></i>
net revenues increased 0.7% as favorable product mix more than offset a volume
decline.&#160; Volume was down 0.9%, as a
decline in Meals was partially offset by growth in <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Oscar Mayer </font></b>meats.&#160; The
decline in Meals volume primarily reflected the exit of certain product lines
in the second half of last year, including <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Kraft</font></b>
Fresh Prep and <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Stove Top</font></b> Oven
Classics.&#160; Oscar Mayer volume was up
behind high single digit growth in cold cuts, as marketing reinvestment spending
continued to drive improved consumption and share, which was up 0.7 points on
the quarter.&#160; Segment OCI decreased
12.4% to $197 million as increased commodity and benefit costs, higher
marketing spending and exit costs for the restructuring program of $9 million
were partially offset by favorable product mix.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:ideograph-numeric ideograph-other;text-decoration:underline;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kraft
International Commercial</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">Operating companies income decreased 26.8% to $191
million, as exit costs for the restructuring program of $34 million, lower
margins, higher benefit costs, infrastructure investment in developing markets,
and an intangible asset impairment charge of $12 million were partially offset
by favorable currency of $24 million. </font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">Net
revenues grew 9.6% to $2,294 million, as favorable currency of $234 million and
pricing actions in response to Latin American devaluation-driven cost increases
were partially offset by increased promotional spending in Europe and the
impact of divestitures.&#160; Volume was down
0.9% due to divestitures, while volume from ongoing businesses was up 0.4%
driven by tack-on acquisitions, which accounted for 2.0 percentage points of
growth.&#160; While growth was solid in
markets such as Germany, the United Kingdom, China and Latin America, overall
growth was impacted by category softness, price competition and trade inventory
reductions in other markets, particularly France, Russia and Puerto Rico. </font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">Following
are first quarter results by segment for KIC:</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Europe, Middle East &amp; Africa (EMEA)</font></u></i> net revenues increased 10.7% as favorable
currency of $208 million was partially offset by the impact of divestitures and
increased promotional spending.&#160; Volume
was down 1.8%, as the impact of divestitures more than offset ongoing volume
growth of 0.5%.&#160; Ongoing volume growth
was driven by tack-on acquisitions and by gains in the United Kingdom and
Germany,</p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">6</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='6',FILE='C:\jms\eudelhofen\04-4571-1\task110594\4571-1-mm.htm',USER='eudelho',CD='Apr 19 11:31 2004' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
</font>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><font style="font-size:10.0pt;">moderated by declines in France, due to
market softness and price competition in coffee, and in Russia, due to trade
inventory reductions. Segment </font>OCI decreased 19.4% to $158
million, reflecting exit costs for the restructuring program of $32 million,
higher benefit costs, infrastructure investment in Eastern Europe and increased
promotional spending, partially offset by favorable currency of $26 million. </font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">EMEA beverages
volume was down. Coffee volume was lower driven primarily by increased price
competition in France, partly offset by growth in Germany and Spain. Refreshment beverages volume decreased,
impacted by reduced <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Tang</font></b> sales in
the Middle East following lower consumption during the Ramadan period. </font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">EMEA snacks
volume was up, as an increase in biscuits, due to acquisitions, was partially
offset by a decline in confectionery, reflecting price competition and trade
inventory reductions in Russia. New products fueled confectionery volume growth
in Germany, Austria and Spain.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">EMEA cheese
volume was lower, impacted by the divestiture of the <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Invernizzi</font></b> business in
Europe. Ongoing cheese volume grew, with gains in the United Kingdom and
Germany driven by the solid performance of <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Philadelphia</font></b> cream cheese. </font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">EMEA grocery
volume increased, with gains in the United Kingdom and in Egypt. EMEA
convenient meals volume was lower, impacted by the divestiture of the <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">reis-fit</font></b>
business in Europe.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><i><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Latin America &amp; Asia Pacific (LAAP)</font></u></i>
net revenues increased 6.3% driven by favorable currency and pricing actions,
partially offset by adverse mix.&#160; Volume
was up 0.4%, as gains in Argentina, Brazil, Venezuela and China were partially
offset by declines in Puerto Rico, Australia and Southeast Asia, with these
markets generally impacted by price competition.&#160; Venezuela&#146;s growth reflects a soft year-ago period when the
country was affected by a national strike.&#160;
Segment OCI decreased 49.2% to $33 million as an intangible asset
impairment charge of $12 million in Mexico, exit costs for the restructuring
program, devaluation-driven cost increases and higher expenses were partially
offset by price increases.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">LAAP snacks volume increased, driven by gains in
Argentina, Brazil, and China, benefiting from new products, and growth in
Venezuela, reflecting a soft year-ago period.&#160;
</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5pt;text-indent:.05pt;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">LAAP beverages volume decreased, as the impact of
price competition in Puerto Rico and Mexico was moderated by a gain in China
behind strong <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Tang</font></b> marketing.&#160; LAAP
cheese and grocery volume grew, driven by gains in Venezuela.</font></p>

<p style="color:#3366FF;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .55pt;text-indent:.05pt;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">*&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; *&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; *</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The company will host a conference call for members of the investment
community at 5:00 p.m. ET on April 19, 2004.&#160;
Access to a live audio webcast is available at www.kraft.com and a replay
of the conference call will be available on the company&#146;s web site.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">7</font></p>


<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kraft Foods Inc. is the largest branded food
and beverage company headquartered in the United States and the second largest
worldwide.&#160; Kraft Foods markets many of
the world&#146;s leading food brands, including <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Kraft</font></b> cheese, <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Jacobs</font></b> and <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Maxwell
House</font></b> coffees, <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Nabisco</font></b> cookies and crackers, <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Philadelphia
</font></b>cream cheese, <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Oscar Mayer</font></b> meats, <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Post</font></b> cereals and <b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Milka</font></b>
chocolates, in more than 150 countries.&#160;
</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<h3 align="center" style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-transform:uppercase;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;text-transform:none;">Forward-Looking and Cautionary Statements</font></u></b></h3>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This press release contains projections of future results and other
forward-looking statements.&#160; </font>One can identify these forward-looking
statements by use of words such as &#147;strategy,&#148; &#147;expects,&#148; &#147;plans,&#148;
&#147;anticipates,&#148; &#147;believes,&#148; &#147;will,&#148; &#147;continues,&#148; &#147;estimates,&#148; &#147;intends,&#148;
&#147;projects,&#148; &#147;goals,&#148; &#147;targets&#148; and other words of similar meaning. One can also
identify them by the fact that they do not relate strictly to historical or
current facts. These statements are based on the company&#146;s assumptions and
estimates and are subject to risks and uncertainties. In connection with the
&#147;safe harbor&#148; provisions of the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of
1995, the company is hereby identifying important factors that could cause
actual results and outcomes to differ materially from those contained in any
forward-looking statement made by or on behalf of the company; any such
statement is qualified by reference to the following cautionary statements. </p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Each
of the company&#146;s segments is subject to intense competition, changes in
consumer preferences and demand for its products, the effects of changing
prices for its raw materials and local economic and market conditions. Their
results are dependent upon their continued ability to promote brand equity
successfully, to anticipate and respond to new consumer trends, to develop new
products and markets, to broaden brand portfolios, to compete effectively with
lower priced products in a consolidating environment at the retail and
manufacturing levels and to improve productivity. The company&#146;s results are
also dependent on its ability to consummate and successfully integrate
acquisitions and to realize the cost savings and improved asset utilization
contemplated by its restructuring program. In addition, the company is subject
to the effects of foreign economies, currency movements, fluctuations in levels
of customer inventories and credit and other business risks related to its
customers operating in a challenging economic and competitive environment. The
company&#146;s results are affected by its access to credit markets, borrowing costs
and credit ratings, which may in turn be influenced by the credit ratings of
Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. The company&#146;s benefit expense is subject to the
investment performance of pension plan assets, interest rates and cost
increases for medical benefits offered to employees and retirees. The food
industry continues to be subject to recalls if products become adulterated or
misbranded, liability if product consumption causes injury, ingredient
disclosure and labeling laws and regulations and the possibility that consumers
could lose confidence in the safety and quality of certain food products. The
food industry is also subject to consumer concerns regarding genetically
modified organisms and the health implications of obesity and trans-fatty
acids. Developments in any of these areas could cause the company&#146;s results to
differ materially from results that have been or</font></p>

</font>

<p align="center" style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;">&nbsp;</p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">KRAFT FOODS INC.<br>
and Subsidiaries<br>
Segment Reclass - Volume</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Quarterly 2003</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(lbs
in millions)</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Note: As a
result of the organization changes announced on January 8, 2004, the company&#146;s
first quarter results are presented in a new segment structure.&#160; Restated historical results are available in
the financial tables contained in this release.&#160; The company reports six segments: U.S. Beverages &amp; Grocery;
U.S. Snacks; U.S. Cheese, Canada &amp; North America Foodservice; U.S.
Convenient Meals; Europe, Middle East &amp; Africa; and Latin America &amp;
Asia Pacific.&#160; The new segment structure
in North America reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between
segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors.&#160; Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico
businesses, which were previously reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers
segment, are now reported in the Latin America &amp; Asia Pacific segment.</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

  </td>
  <td width="2%" valign="bottom" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:2.0%;">
  <p style="font-size:1.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;">&nbsp;</p>
  </td>
  <td width="11%" valign="bottom" style="border:none;border-bottom:solid windowtext .5pt;padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:11.0%;">
  <p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:8.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Q2</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="font-family:'Times New Roman';font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;">&nbsp;</p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">KRAFT FOODS INC.<br>
and Subsidiaries<br>
Segment Reclass - Net Revenues</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Quarterly 2003</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">($
in millions)</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Note: As a
result of the organization changes announced on January 8, 2004, the company&#146;s
first quarter results are presented in a new segment structure.&#160; Restated historical results are available in
the financial tables contained in this release.&#160; The company reports six segments: U.S. Beverages &amp; Grocery;
U.S. Snacks; U.S. Cheese, Canada &amp; North America Foodservice; U.S.
Convenient Meals; Europe, Middle East &amp; Africa; and Latin America &amp;
Asia Pacific.&#160; The new segment structure
in North America reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between
segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors.&#160; Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico
businesses, which were previously reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers
segment, are now reported in the Latin America &amp; Asia Pacific segment.</font></i></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">KRAFT
FOODS INC.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">and
Subsidiaries</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Segment
Reclass - Operating Companies Income</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Quarterly 2003</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">($
in millions)</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 204.0pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Note: As a
result of the organization changes announced on January 8, 2004, the company&#146;s
first quarter results are presented in a new segment structure.&#160; Restated historical results are available in
the financial tables contained in this release.&#160; The company reports six segments: U.S. Beverages &amp; Grocery;
U.S. Snacks; U.S. Cheese, Canada &amp; North America Foodservice; U.S.
Convenient Meals; Europe, Middle East &amp; Africa; and Latin America &amp;
Asia Pacific.&#160; The new segment structure
in North America reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between
segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors.&#160; Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico
businesses, which were previously reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers
segment, are now reported in the Latin America &amp; Asia Pacific segment.</font></i></p>
